name: using-superpowers
description: Use when starting any conversation - establishes how to find and use skills, requiring Skill tool invocation before ANY response including clarifying questions
---
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
<SUBAGENT-STOP>
If you were dispatched as a subagent to execute a specific task, skip this skill.
</SUBAGENT-STOP>
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
<EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT>
If you think there is even a 1% chance a skill might apply to what you are doing, you ABSOLUTELY MUST invoke the skill.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
IF A SKILL APPLIES TO YOUR TASK, YOU DO NOT HAVE A CHOICE. YOU MUST USE IT.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
This is not negotiable. This is not optional. You cannot rationalize your way out of this.
</EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT>
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Instruction Priority
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Superpowers skills override default system prompt behavior, but **user instructions always take precedence**:
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
1. **User's explicit instructions** (CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, AGENTS.md, direct requests) ╞Æ?" highest priority
2. **Superpowers skills** ╞Æ?" override default system behavior where they conflict
3. **Default system prompt** ╞Æ?" lowest priority
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
If CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, or AGENTS.md says "don't use TDD" and a skill says "always use TDD," follow the user's instructions. The user is in control.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## How to Access Skills
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**In Claude Code:** Use the `Skill` tool. When you invoke a skill, its content is loaded and presented to you╞Æ?"follow it directly. Never use the Read tool on skill files.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**In Copilot CLI:** Use the `skill` tool. Skills are auto-discovered from installed plugins. The `skill` tool works the same as Claude Code's `Skill` tool.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**In Gemini CLI:** Skills activate via the `activate_skill` tool. Gemini loads skill metadata at session start and activates the full content on demand.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**In other environments:** Check your platform's documentation for how skills are loaded.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Platform Adaptation
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Skills use Claude Code tool names. Non-CC platforms: see `references/copilot-tools.md` (Copilot CLI), `references/codex-tools.md` (Codex) for tool equivalents. Gemini CLI users get the tool mapping loaded automatically via GEMINI.md.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
# Using Skills
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## The Rule
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Invoke relevant or requested skills BEFORE any response or action.** Even a 1% chance a skill might apply means that you should invoke the skill to check. If an invoked skill turns out to be wrong for the situation, you don't need to use it.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
```dot
digraph skill_flow {
    "User message received" [shape=doublecircle];
    "About to EnterPlanMode?" [shape=doublecircle];
    "Already brainstormed?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke brainstorming skill" [shape=box];
    "Might any skill apply?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke Skill tool" [shape=box];
    "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'" [shape=box];
    "Has checklist?" [shape=diamond];
    "Create TodoWrite todo per item" [shape=box];
    "Follow skill exactly" [shape=box];
    "Respond (including clarifications)" [shape=doublecircle];
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
    "About to EnterPlanMode?" -> "Already brainstormed?";
    "Already brainstormed?" -> "Invoke brainstorming skill" [label="no"];
    "Already brainstormed?" -> "Might any skill apply?" [label="yes"];
    "Invoke brainstorming skill" -> "Might any skill apply?";
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
    "User message received" -> "Might any skill apply?";
    "Might any skill apply?" -> "Invoke Skill tool" [label="yes, even 1%"];
    "Might any skill apply?" -> "Respond (including clarifications)" [label="definitely not"];
    "Invoke Skill tool" -> "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'";
    "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'" -> "Has checklist?";
    "Has checklist?" -> "Create TodoWrite todo per item" [label="yes"];
    "Has checklist?" -> "Follow skill exactly" [label="no"];
    "Create TodoWrite todo per item" -> "Follow skill exactly";
}
```
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Red Flags
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
These thoughts mean STOP╞Æ?"you're rationalizing:
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
| Thought | Reality |
|---------|---------|
| "This is just a simple question" | Questions are tasks. Check for skills. |
| "I need more context first" | Skill check comes BEFORE clarifying questions. |
| "Let me explore the codebase first" | Skills tell you HOW to explore. Check first. |
| "I can check git/files quickly" | Files lack conversation context. Check for skills. |
| "Let me gather information first" | Skills tell you HOW to gather information. |
| "This doesn't need a formal skill" | If a skill exists, use it. |
| "I remember this skill" | Skills evolve. Read current version. |
| "This doesn't count as a task" | Action = task. Check for skills. |
| "The skill is overkill" | Simple things become complex. Use it. |
| "I'll just do this one thing first" | Check BEFORE doing anything. |
| "This feels productive" | Undisciplined action wastes time. Skills prevent this. |
| "I know what that means" | Knowing the concept ╞Æ%├┐ using the skill. Invoke it. |
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Skill Priority
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
When multiple skills could apply, use this order:
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
1. **Process skills first** (brainstorming, debugging) - these determine HOW to approach the task
2. **Implementation skills second** (frontend-design, mcp-builder) - these guide execution
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
"Let's build X" ╞Æ+' brainstorming first, then implementation skills.
"Fix this bug" ╞Æ+' debugging first, then domain-specific skills.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Skill Types
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Rigid** (TDD, debugging): Follow exactly. Don't adapt away discipline.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Flexible** (patterns): Adapt principles to context.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
The skill itself tells you which.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## User Instructions
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Instructions say WHAT, not HOW. "Add X" or "Fix Y" doesn't mean skip workflows.

# Spec 7 Bundle Corpus Index Plan Review - Iteration 2
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Scope:** v2 implementation plan, accepted design type correction, and verification against `docs/reviews/bundle-corpus-index/2026-04-27/plan-1/REVIEW.md`.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Verdict:** Rejected. Opus accepted, but both Codex reviewers found remaining concrete gaps. The findings are bounded and should be fixed in v3.

Claude was reachable and returned `ACCEPT`.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Findings
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### High - `failedTicks` freeze snippet does not typecheck as written
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-1 found that `makeEntry()` freezes `failedTicks` into a `readonly number[]` and then assigns it into `Readonly<SessionMetadata>`, whose nested array type remains `number[]`. That snippet can fail typecheck unless the plan specifies a narrow runtime-freeze cast or changes the public metadata type.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Keep the accepted public type `Readonly<SessionMetadata>` and update the plan snippet to build a frozen defensive array, then assign it through a narrow `as number[]` cast:
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
```ts
const frozenFailedTicks = manifest.metadata.failedTicks
  ? Object.freeze(manifest.metadata.failedTicks.slice())
  : undefined;
const metadata: Readonly<SessionMetadata> = Object.freeze({
  ...manifest.metadata,
  ...(frozenFailedTicks ? { failedTicks: frozenFailedTicks as number[] } : {}),
});
```
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
This preserves the runtime contract while staying compatible with the existing `SessionMetadata` type.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Missing test coverage for `failedTicks` immutability
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Both Codex reviewers found that the v2 plan tests top-level metadata freezing but not the nested `failedTicks` defensive copy/freeze requirement.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add assertions in the incomplete-bundle test that `metadata.failedTicks` is frozen, mutation throws, and later `entries()` results still expose the original `[26, 27]` list.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Missing explicit `incomplete` query coverage
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 found that the test plan still does not assert `entries({ incomplete: true })` or `entries({ incomplete: false })`, even though the accepted design lists `incomplete` as a covered query filter.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add positive and negative incomplete-filter assertions to the incomplete-bundle test.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Doc audit still omits some exported public names and runs before final docs
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 found that the audit pattern omits several public exports: `BundleCorpusScanDepth`, `BundleCorpusOptions`, `NumberRange`, `IsoTimeRange`, `CorpusIndexErrorCode`, `CorpusIndexErrorDetails`, and `InvalidCorpusEntry`. It also runs before final devlog edits, so it does not audit the final committed docs state.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Expand the audit pattern to every public export and rerun the audit after final devlog updates, before the final gates/commit.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException

# Spec 7 Bundle Corpus Index Plan Review - Iteration 1
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Scope:** `docs/design/2026-04-27-bundle-corpus-index-implementation-plan.md` plus the accepted Spec 7 design context.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Verdict:** Rejected. The plan is directionally sound, but reviewers found one typecheck blocker and several concrete test/process/doc gaps that need a v2 plan before coding starts.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Raw Outputs
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- `raw/codex.md`
- `raw/codex-2.md`
- `raw/opus.md`
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Claude was reachable for this iteration.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Findings
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### High - `CorpusIndexErrorDetails` shape is not assignable to `JsonValue`
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 and Opus both found that the planned interface combines `readonly [key: string]: JsonValue` with optional `path`, `key`, and `message` fields. Optional properties include `undefined`, which is not a `JsonValue`. Opus also noted that overriding `SessionRecordingError.details` with that shape fails because the base property is `JsonValue | undefined`.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Change the design and plan to use a JSON-safe details object with required nullable fields:
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
```ts
export interface CorpusIndexErrorDetails {
  readonly [key: string]: JsonValue;
  readonly code: CorpusIndexErrorCode;
  readonly path: string | null;
  readonly key: string | null;
  readonly message: string | null;
}
```
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Use an internal `CorpusIndexErrorDetailsInput` helper and `normalizeDetails()` so call sites can keep passing concise optional fields while the public `details` object remains JSON-shaped.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - `attachmentMime` any-match behavior is under-tested
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Both Codex passes found that the planned tests only cover a single-attachment PNG bundle. That would not catch an implementation that treats `attachmentMime` as exact-set or all-match, even though the accepted design requires a multi-attachment proof.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add a test with at least two MIME types, assert single MIME and one-of-many positive matches, and assert a negative no-overlap case.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - `key: RegExp` can be stateful for `/g` and `/y`
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Both Codex passes found that calling `query.key.test(entry.key)` directly lets global or sticky regex `lastIndex` state leak across entries.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add global-regex test coverage and implement a `matchesKey()` helper that resets `lastIndex` before and after each test.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Doc audit is too narrow
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-1 found that the planned doc audit scans only a handpicked subset of docs. The accepted design requires a doc-review or grep across `docs/` and `README.md`, while historical changelog/devlog/drift-log context can remain.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Replace the narrow audit with an all-markdown docs scan plus README scan for new API names. Since Spec 7 is additive, explicitly state that there are no removed/renamed API names to grep.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Accepted-design callouts are missing from concrete doc tasks
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 found that the docs plan does not explicitly require `materializedEndTick` to be documented as a persisted-content horizon rather than a replay guarantee, and does not explicitly require embedded `dataUrl` attachments to be documented as manifest parse cost rather than content indexing.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add guide/API/changelog tasks for incomplete-bundle behavior and embedded dataUrl attachment cost.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Test-count expectation is stale-prone
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 noted that hardcoding the current pass count makes the plan fragile and may already conflict with current docs.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Replace the expected full-suite count with "all tests pass and existing todo tests remain todo."
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Review artifacts need re-staging after generation
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 and Opus found that the plan stages `docs/reviews/bundle-corpus-index-T1` before review files are generated, but does not explicitly stage the newly written raw/diff/REVIEW files before commit.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add a re-stage step after each code-review iteration and before final verification.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Low - Two-Codex reviewer setup needs a handoff note
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Opus objected that `raw/codex-2.md` is not the AGENTS.md default. The handoff explicitly requires two separate Codex review passes because Claude quota may be limited.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Keep `raw/codex-2.md`, but add a note that this follows the current handoff and supplements Claude when reachable.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Low - `OneOrMany<T>` export mismatch
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Opus noted that the accepted design snippet exports `OneOrMany<T>`, while the implementation plan kept it module-private and omitted it from `src/index.ts`.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Export `OneOrMany<T>` and include it in docs/API/export checklist.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Low - Devlog summary compaction needs a concrete action
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Opus noted that the plan says to keep the summary under 50 lines, but the file is already above that threshold.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add a concrete compaction instruction for `docs/devlog/summary.md` while preserving newest-first status lines.

## Findings
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - README and roadmap tasks still allow stale "Spec 7 is future" language
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-1 found that the plan says to add a README row and mark the roadmap implemented, but does not explicitly remove current stale language that describes corpus indexing as future Tier-2 work or Spec 7 as proposed/not drafted.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Make the README and roadmap tasks require scrubbing stale future/proposed language: update the Synthetic Playtest README row, add the Bundle Corpus row, fix public surface bullets, revise the Spec 7 roadmap section, and update the status tracker from proposed/not drafted to implemented v0.8.3.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Behavioral metrics guide task does not replace in-memory-only framing
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-1 found that the plan only adds a disk-backed example, while the accepted design says to replace in-memory-only corpus examples with a disk-backed `BundleCorpus` example.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Update the plan so `docs/guides/behavioral-metrics.md` uses `BundleCorpus` as the primary quickstart/framing and keeps in-memory arrays only as an optional small-test pattern.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### High - Public ordering snippets use locale-dependent `localeCompare`
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 found `localeCompare()` in entry sorting, attachment MIME sorting, and child discovery sorting. Default locale collation can vary across hosts, which weakens deterministic CI ordering.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add a locale-independent `compareCodeUnit()` helper using `<` / `>` comparisons, use it for all public ordering, and add a tie-order regression test that would fail under locale-dependent case collation.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Lazy bundle iteration is not proven
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 found that the planned lazy-loading test does not catch eager materialization. A `bundles()` implementation that loads all matching bundles before yielding the first one could pass.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add a test with first bundle valid and second bundle malformed. Assert the first `iterator.next()` succeeds and only the second `iterator.next()` throws.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Medium - Stop-descending-inside-bundle discovery is not proven
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Codex-2 found that tests cover scan-depth limits but not the accepted contract that discovery stops once a directory is identified as a bundle directory.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Action:** Add a fixture with a nested `manifest.json` under an already indexed bundle directory and assert only the outer bundle key is indexed.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException

# Architecture
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Overview
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Civ-engine is a general-purpose, headless, AI-native 2D grid-based game engine. Built in Node.js/TypeScript with a strict ECS (Entity-Component-System) architecture.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**AI-native** means the engine is designed to be operated by AI agents, not human players directly. Humans provide high-level game designs; AI agents write game logic, submit commands, and observe state. Every design decision prioritizes machine-readability: deterministic tick execution, JSON-serializable state, structured diffs, typed command/event interfaces, and a purely programmatic API with no interactive UI.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
The engine provides reusable infrastructure (entities, components, spatial indexing, events, commands, resources, serialization) that game projects consume. It outputs state changes that a separate client can render; it contains no game-specific logic, rendering, or UI code.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Component Map
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
| Component      | File                     | Responsibility                                                                         |
| -------------- | ------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| World          | `src/world.ts`           | Top-level API, owns all subsystems, phased system pipeline, metrics, spatial index sync |
| EntityManager  | `src/entity-manager.ts`  | Entity creation/destruction, ID recycling via free-list, generation counters           |
| ComponentStore | `src/component-store.ts` | Sparse array storage per component type, generation counter for change detection       |
| SpatialGrid    | `src/spatial-grid.ts`    | Sparse occupied-cell grid plus read-only view, neighbor/radius queries                 |
| GameLoop       | `src/game-loop.ts`       | Fixed-timestep loop, step() for testing, start()/stop() for real-time, speed multiplier, pause/resume |
| EventBus       | `src/event-bus.ts`       | Typed pub/sub event bus, per-tick buffer, listener registry                            |
| CommandQueue   | `src/command-queue.ts`   | Typed command buffer, push/drain interface                                             |
| CommandTransaction | `src/command-transaction.ts` | Atomic propose-validate-commit-or-abort builder over World; buffers component/position/resource mutations + events + precondition predicates, applies all-or-nothing on `commit()` |
| Serializer     | `src/serializer.ts`      | Versioned WorldSnapshot types for state serialization                                  |
| Diff           | `src/diff.ts`            | TickDiff type for per-tick change sets                                                 |
| ResourceStore  | `src/resource-store.ts`  | Resource pools, production/consumption rates, transfers, dirty tracking                |
| OccupancyGrid  | `src/occupancy-grid.ts`  | Deterministic blocked-cell, footprint, reservation, lifecycle binding, blocker metadata, metrics, and sub-cell crowding tracking |
| Layer          | `src/layer.ts`           | Generic typed overlay map at configurable downsampled resolution; sparse cell storage with default-value semantics, JSON-serializable; multi-resolution field data (pollution, influence, weather, danger, etc.) |
| JSON helpers   | `src/json.ts`            | JSON-compatible component validation and fingerprints for mutation detection           |
| Noise          | `src/noise.ts`           | Seedable 2D simplex noise, octave layering utility                                     |
| Cellular       | `src/cellular.ts`        | Cellular automata step function, immutable CellGrid                                    |
| MapGen         | `src/map-gen.ts`         | MapGenerator interface, createTileGrid bulk tile-entity helper                         |
| Pathfinding    | `src/pathfinding.ts`     | Generic A* pathfinding, graph-agnostic with user-defined callbacks          |
| Path Service   | `src/path-service.ts`    | Grid path helper, deterministic path queue, and cache for batched request handling     |
| RenderAdapter  | `src/render-adapter.ts`  | Projects world state into renderer-facing snapshots and diffs with generation-aware refs |
| ScenarioRunner | `src/scenario-runner.ts` | Headless setup/run/check harness built on World, WorldDebugger, and WorldHistoryRecorder |
| VisibilityMap  | `src/visibility-map.ts`  | Per-player visible/explored cell tracking for fog-of-war style mechanics               |
| WorldDebugger  | `src/world-debugger.ts`  | Structured debug snapshots, warnings, and probe helpers for engine and standalone utilities |
| ClientAdapter  | `src/client-adapter.ts`  | Bridges World API to typed client messages via send callback |
| BehaviorTree   | `src/behavior-tree.ts`   | Generic BT framework: NodeStatus, BTNode, Selector, Sequence, ReactiveSelector, ReactiveSequence, Action, Condition, BTState, createBehaviorTree, clearRunningState |
| SessionRecorder | `src/session-recorder.ts` | Captures live World runs into SessionBundle via SessionSink; mutex-locked single payload-capturing recorder per world (slot at world.__payloadCapturingRecorder); marker validation per spec A6.1; terminal snapshot on disconnect |
| SessionReplayer | `src/session-replayer.ts` | Loads a SessionBundle/Source; openAt(tick) returns paused World; selfCheck() 3-stream comparison (state via deepEqualWithPath, events, executions); failedTicks-skipping; cross-b/cross-Node-major version checks |
| SessionBundle / SessionSink / SessionSource / Marker / RecordedCommand | `src/session-bundle.ts`, `src/session-sink.ts`, `src/session-file-sink.ts` | Shared bundle types + sink/source interfaces + MemorySink + FileSink (disk-backed; manifest atomic-rename; defaults to sidecar attachments). scenarioResultToBundle adapter at `src/session-scenario-bundle.ts`. |
| Synthetic Playtest Harness | `src/synthetic-playtest.ts` | Tier-1 autonomous-driver primitive: `runSynthPlaytest` drives a `World` via pluggable `Policy` functions for N ticks ╞Æ+' `SessionBundle`. Sub-RNG (`PolicyContext.random()`) sandboxed from `world.rng`, seeded from `policySeed`. Built-in policies: `noopPolicy`, `randomPolicy`, `scriptedPolicy`. Composes with `SessionRecorder`/`SessionReplayer`. New in v0.7.20 + v0.8.0 + v0.8.1 (Spec 3). |
| Behavioral Metrics | `src/behavioral-metrics.ts` | Tier-2 corpus reducer over `Iterable<SessionBundle>`. Accumulator-style `Metric<TState, TResult>` contract; 11 engine-generic built-in metrics (`bundleCount`, `sessionLengthStats`, etc.); pure-function `runMetrics` + `compareMetricsResults` delta helper. New in v0.8.2 (Spec 8). |
| Public exports | `src/index.ts`           | Barrel export for the intended package API                                             |
| Types          | `src/types.ts`           | Shared type definitions (EntityId, EntityRef, Position, WorldConfig, InstrumentationProfile) |
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Data Flow
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
```
World.step()
  -> GameLoop.step()
    -> World.executeTick()
      -> World.eventBus.clear()       [reset buffer from previous tick]
      -> World.entityManager.clearDirty()
      -> World.clearComponentDirty()   [clear dirty flags on all stores]
      -> World.processCommands()       [drain queue, run handlers]
      -> input systems
      -> preUpdate systems
      -> update systems
      -> postUpdate systems
      -> output systems
      -> World.resourceStore.processTick()  [production, consumption, transfers]
      -> World.buildDiff()             [collect dirty state into TickDiff]
      -> World.getMetrics() state updated   [detailed in `full`, coarse in `minimal`, skipped by implicit `step()` in `release`]
      -> notify onDiff listeners
    -> tick++
```
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spatial Index Sync
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Position writes through `world.setPosition()` or `world.setComponent()` with the configured position component (default `'position'`, configurable via `positionKey` in `WorldConfig`) update the component store and spatial grid in lockstep ╞Æ?" the grid stays consistent without any per-tick scan. In-place mutation of position objects (e.g. `world.getComponent(id, 'position').x = 5`) is **not** auto-detected and is a no-op for the grid; game code must call `setPosition` for movement to take effect.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Entity Destruction
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
`destroyEntity(id)` performs immediate cleanup:
- Removes entity from grid using `previousPositions` (the grid's last-seen position, kept in sync by `setPosition`)
- Removes all components from all stores
- Removes all resource pools, rates, and transfers for the entity
- Marks entity as dead in EntityManager (ID available for recycling)
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Boundaries
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- **World** is the only public entry point. EntityManager, ComponentStore, GameLoop are internal implementation details.
- **Systems** are pure functions `(world: World) => void` or registration objects with a `phase` and `name`. Phases are intentionally lightweight and ordered as `input`, `preUpdate`, `update`, `postUpdate`, `output`.
- **Components** are pure data interfaces. No methods, no inheritance.
- **SpatialGrid** is a sparse map of occupied cells. The grid is updated lock-step with position writes ╞Æ?" every `world.setPosition` / `world.setComponent` on the configured `positionKey` inserts/moves the entity in the grid in the same call, so no per-tick scan is needed. User systems read grid state via `world.grid.getAt()` / `world.grid.getNeighbors()` / `world.grid.getInRadius()`. The `world.grid` property is a read-only delegate at runtime: `getAt()` returns a fresh `Set` copy on each call, the mutating `insert`/`remove`/`move` methods of the underlying `SpatialGrid` are not exposed, and the delegate object itself is `Object.freeze`d in the constructor (since v0.7.3) so attempts to monkey-patch its methods throw `TypeError` in strict mode. This makes the read-only-delegate promise structural rather than convention-only.
- **GameLoop** handles timing only. It knows nothing about entities, components, or systems.
- **EventBus** is owned by World. Systems emit and subscribe via `world.emit()` / `world.on()`. External consumers read events via `world.getEvents()` between ticks. Do not call `eventBus.clear()` directly ╞Æ?" World handles this.
- **CommandQueue** is owned by World. External code submits commands via `world.submit()` or `world.submitWithResult()`, registers validators via `world.registerValidator()`, and registers handlers via `world.registerHandler()`. Do not access the queue directly.
- **CommandTransaction** is a synchronous builder created via `world.transaction()`. It is generic over `<TEventMap, TCommandMap, TComponents, TState>` (matching `World`'s generic order); typed component / state access works inside the transaction the same way it works inside `world.setComponent` / `world.setState`. The transaction buffers proposed mutations (`setComponent`/`addComponent`/`patchComponent`/`removeComponent`/`setPosition`/`addResource`/`removeResource`), buffered events (`emit` ╞Æ?" JSON-compat validated at buffer time, not at commit), and `require()` precondition predicates. **Predicates receive a `ReadOnlyTransactionWorld` faAade**, not the live `World` ╞Æ?" write methods (`setComponent`, `setState`, `emit`, `addResource`, `removeResource`, `destroyEntity`, etc.) are excluded at the type level and rejected at runtime so a side-effecting predicate cannot violate the "world untouched on precondition failure" guarantee. On `commit()` the engine calls `world.warnIfPoisoned('transaction')` (warns once per poison cycle), then runs all preconditions in registration order; if any returns `false` or a string, no mutation or event is applied and the transaction returns `{ ok: false, code: 'precondition_failed', reason }`. Otherwise mutations are applied to the world in registration order via the existing public mutation API (so they get the same liveness/JSON-compat validation as direct calls), then events are emitted via `EventBus`. Transactions are single-use: `commit()` after a previous `commit()` throws; `commit()` after `abort()` returns `{ ok: false, code: 'aborted' }` without mutation, and subsequent builder calls throw an "already aborted" error (not "already committed"). If a buffered mutation throws mid-commit, the transaction is still consumed (status flips to `committed` in a `finally` block) so the caller cannot retry and double-apply earlier mutations ╞Æ?" the world is in a partially-applied state that the caller must reconcile. Reads inside a precondition or after commit see live world state; transactions do not provide a "shadow" overlay view of their own proposed mutations. Buffered values are stored by reference; caller must not mutate buffered objects between buffering and `commit()`. Entity create/destroy, tags, metadata, and world-state writes are not yet wrapped (v1 surface).
- **Serialization** is accessed via `world.serialize()` and `World.deserialize()`. Snapshot version 5 (WorldSnapshotV5) is the current write format and additionally round-trips per-component `ComponentStoreOptions` (the `componentOptions` field) so `diffMode` survives save/load; version 4 includes state, tags, and metadata; version 3 includes resource state and deterministic RNG state; versions 1 and 2 remain readable for compatibility. `WorldConfig.maxTicksPerFrame` and `WorldConfig.instrumentationProfile` are also serialized when non-default. The `WorldSnapshot` type is exported from `src/serializer.ts`. Snapshots are plain JSON-serializable objects, and component data plus state values are `structuredClone`d at both serialize and deserialize boundaries so callers cannot write through.
- **State Diffs** are accessed via `world.getDiff()` (pull) or `world.onDiff()` (push). The `TickDiff` type is exported from `src/diff.ts`. Diffs capture entity creation/destruction, component mutations, and resource changes per tick. `getDiff()` returns a JSON-deep-cloned defensive copy ╞Æ?" callers cannot write through to live engine state. During `onDiff` listeners `world.tick === diff.tick`.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- **Tick failure semantics** are fail-fast. A failure in any tick phase (commands, systems, resources, diff, listeners) marks the world as **poisoned**. While poisoned, `world.step()` throws `WorldTickFailureError` and `world.stepWithResult()` returns a `world_poisoned` failure result. `world.isPoisoned()` reports the state; `world.recover()` clears the poison flag along with the cached `lastTickFailure`/`currentDiff`/`currentMetrics`. Failed ticks consume a tick number ╞Æ?" if a tick fails at tick `N+1`, the next successful tick after `recover()` is `N+2`, so failed-tick events and successful-tick events never share a tick number.
- **Metrics** are accessed via `world.getMetrics()` after a tick. They report section timings, per-system timings, query cache hit/miss counts, entity counts, and explicit-sync counts (`spatial.explicitSyncs`, incremented by every `setPosition`-style write). `instrumentationProfile: 'full'` keeps the detailed implicit metrics path, `minimal` keeps coarse implicit metrics, and `release` disables implicit metrics collection on `step()` so shipping runtimes do not pay that cost unless they explicitly use `stepWithResult()`.
- **Rendering** belongs outside the engine. Renderer clients should consume snapshots and tick diffs through `ClientAdapter`, keep visual objects in renderer-owned state, and submit input back as commands. See `docs/guides/rendering.md` for the recommended renderer boundary and Pixi-first reference client shape.
- **RenderAdapter** is an optional projection helper. It turns current world state plus `TickDiff` into renderer-facing `renderSnapshot` and `renderTick` messages using game-owned callbacks. It does not own renderer objects or backend assumptions.
- **Resources** are managed via `world.registerResource()`, `world.addResource()`, `world.removeResource()`, etc. The ResourceStore is owned by World as a private subsystem. Resource rates and transfers are processed automatically after user systems each tick.
- **Noise, Cellular, MapGen** are standalone utilities. They are not owned by World and have no integration point in the tick loop. Game code imports them directly and uses them during setup (before the simulation runs).
- **OccupancyGrid** is a standalone utility. It models blocked cells, occupied footprints, and temporary reservations. `OccupancyBinding` composes it with blocker metadata, destroy-time cleanup hooks, optional sub-cell crowding, and scan metrics when game code wants a higher-level passability surface. These occupancy helpers remain intentionally separate from `SpatialGrid`, which answers proximity rather than passability.
- **Layer** is a standalone typed overlay map. `Layer<T>` represents field data at a configurable downsampled resolution (e.g., a `pollution` map at half-res of the world, or an `influence` map at quarter-res). World coordinates are auto-bucketed via `getAt(worldX, worldY)` / `setAt(worldX, worldY, value)`; cell coordinates are accessible via `getCell` / `setCell`. Storage is **strip-at-write sparse**: writes equal to `defaultValue` delete the underlying entry instead of storing a marker, so the in-memory map and the serialized form agree without a `getState` round-trip. Explicit `clear(cx, cy)` / `clearAt(wx, wy)` methods provide an honest "drop this cell" API. Defensive copies on every read/write boundary protect callers from internal-state aliasing for object `T`; for **primitive `T`** (`number`, `string`, `boolean`, `null`) clones are skipped because primitives are immutable on the JS side, making `Layer<number>` etc. zero-allocation across reads and writes. `forEachReadOnly(cb)` is an explicit zero-allocation read path for object `T` consumers who own the no-mutate discipline. Layers are JSON-serializable through `getState()` / `Layer.fromState()` and value writes are validated via `assertJsonCompatible`. Layers are independent of `World`; game code instantiates and ticks them from systems. They are a sibling utility to `OccupancyGrid` and `VisibilityMap` ╞Æ?" the engine does not own per-game field data, only the data structure.
- **Pathfinding** is a standalone utility. It has no knowledge of the spatial grid, entities, or the tick loop. Game code provides `neighbors`, `cost`, `heuristic`, and `hash` callbacks to wire it to any graph topology.
- **Path Service** is a standalone utility built on top of `findPath`. It provides `findGridPath`, `PathCache`, `PathRequestQueue`, and `createGridPathQueue` for deterministic batched path processing.
- **VisibilityMap** is a standalone utility. It tracks per-player visible and explored cells and remains independent of rendering and UI code.
- **WorldDebugger** is a standalone inspection utility. It captures structured summaries of world state, metrics, events, last-diff data, and custom probe output for standalone utilities such as occupancy, visibility, and path queues.
- **ScenarioRunner** is a standalone orchestration utility. It pairs prepared setup, deterministic stepping, checks, debugger output, and short-horizon history into one machine-readable result for AI agents and harnesses.
- **BehaviorTree** is a standalone utility. It has no knowledge of World, entities, or the tick loop. Game code defines tree structure via `createBehaviorTree`, stores `BTState` as a component, and ticks trees from a system. The `TContext` generic is game-defined ╞Æ?" the engine does not prescribe what context contains beyond a BTState accessor. Reactive variants (`reactiveSelector`, `reactiveSequence`) re-evaluate from the root each tick without persisting running state; `clearRunningState` provides imperative subtree resets.
- **ClientAdapter** reads World state and subscribes to diffs. It does not modify World internals directly ╞Æ?" it uses only the public API (`serialize`, `onDiff`/`offDiff`, `getEvents`, `submitWithResult`).
- **World State** is owned by World as a private Map. Systems read/write via `world.setState()`/`world.getState()`. State is non-entity structured data (terrain config, simulation time, etc.). Typed against the `TState` generic on `World` (default `Record<string, unknown>`) ╞Æ?" independent of the `TComponents` registry. Included in serialization and diffs.
- **Tags & Metadata** are owned by World. Tags are string labels with reverse-index lookup via `world.getByTag()`. Metadata is key-value per entity with unique reverse-index via `world.getByMeta()` ╞Æ?" `setMeta` throws if another live entity already owns the `(key, value)` pair. Both cleaned up on entity destruction; the cleanup is reflected in `TickDiff.tags`/`TickDiff.metadata` as `{ entity, tags: [] }` / `{ entity, meta: {} }`.
- **System Ordering** supports optional `before`/`after` named constraints in `SystemRegistration`. Constraints resolve via topological sort within each phase at first tick (or after dynamic registration). Cross-phase constraints are errors.
- **Session Recording** is a dedicated subsystem (`src/session-recorder.ts`, `src/session-replayer.ts`, `src/session-bundle.ts`, `src/session-sink.ts`, `src/session-file-sink.ts`, `src/session-scenario-bundle.ts`, `src/session-errors.ts`) that captures deterministic, replayable bundles of any World run. Per ADR 1, it runs as a sibling to `WorldHistoryRecorder` rather than extending it ╞Æ?" the two recorders have different shapes (rolling debug buffer vs. persistent archive) and different consumers. `WorldHistoryRecorder` continues to serve in-process debugging; `SessionRecorder` is for archive + replay. **Mutex:** payload-capturing recorders (any `SessionRecorder`, OR `WorldHistoryRecorder({ captureCommandPayloads: true })`) are mutually exclusive on a given world (one wrap on `submitWithResult` per world); default-config `WorldHistoryRecorder` instances compose freely. The `world.__payloadCapturingRecorder` slot enforces this. **Replay** uses the `World.applySnapshot(snap)` instance method (added in T0 of the implementation): `worldFactory` must register components/handlers on a fresh world, then call `applySnapshot` in-place ╞Æ?" `World.deserialize` would conflict with subsequent re-registration. Replay across recorded `TickFailure` is out of scope for v1 (`WorldSnapshotV5` doesn't carry poison state); future spec extends to v6. **Determinism contract** (spec A11) is documented but NOT structurally enforced; `SessionReplayer.selfCheck()` is the verification mechanism. See `docs/guides/session-recording.md` for the user-facing guide.

1:# Bundle Corpus Index Implementation Plan
2:
3:> **For agentic workers:** REQUIRED SUB-SKILL: Use superpowers:subagent-driven-development (recommended) or superpowers:executing-plans to implement this plan task-by-task. Steps use checkbox (`- [ ]`) syntax for tracking.
4:
5:**Plan revision:** v4 (2026-04-27) - fixes plan-review iteration 3 findings from `docs/reviews/bundle-corpus-index/2026-04-27/plan-3/`: stale README/roadmap cleanup, BundleCorpus-first behavioral-metrics docs, locale-independent ordering, proven lazy bundle loading, and stop-descending discovery coverage.
6:
7:**Goal:** Implement Spec 7: Bundle Search / Corpus Index as a disk-backed manifest-first `BundleCorpus` that indexes closed FileSink bundle directories, filters metadata without loading content streams, and yields `SessionBundle`s lazily for `runMetrics`.
8:
9:**Architecture:** Add one focused module, `src/bundle-corpus.ts`, that owns filesystem discovery, manifest validation, immutable entry construction, query validation/filtering, and FileSink-backed bundle/source loading. The new module composes with existing session recording, FileSink, SessionReplayer, and behavioral metrics without changing their signatures.
10:
11:**Tech Stack:** TypeScript 5.7+, Node `fs`/`path`, Vitest 3, ESLint 9, ESM + Node16 module resolution.
12:
13:**Branch:** None. Commit directly to `main` after plan review, implementation, full gates, staged multi-CLI code review, and final doc updates.
14:
15:**Versioning:** Base is v0.8.2. Spec 7 is additive and non-breaking, so ship v0.8.3 with one coherent commit.

53:### Step 1: Write failing corpus tests first

55:- [ ] Create `tests/bundle-corpus.test.ts` with FileSink-backed fixtures. Use canonical UTC `recordedAt` values because corpus construction validates UTC-Z strings.
56:
57:```ts
58:import { mkdtempSync, rmSync, writeFileSync, mkdirSync, symlinkSync } from 'node:fs';
59:import { join } from 'node:path';
60:import { tmpdir } from 'node:os';
61:import { afterEach, describe, expect, it } from 'vitest';
62:import {
63:  BundleCorpus,
64:  CorpusIndexError,
65:  FileSink,
66:  SessionRecordingError,
67:  bundleCount,
68:  runMetrics,
69:  type AttachmentDescriptor,
70:  type SessionMetadata,
71:  type SessionSnapshotEntry,
72:} from '../src/index.js';
73:
74:const roots: string[] = [];
75:
76:function tempRoot(): string {
77:  const root = mkdtempSync(join(tmpdir(), 'civ-engine-corpus-'));
78:  roots.push(root);
79:  return root;
80:}
81:
82:afterEach(() => {
83:  for (const root of roots.splice(0)) {
84:    rmSync(root, { recursive: true, force: true });
85:  }
86:});
87:
88:function metadata(id: string, overrides: Partial<SessionMetadata> = {}): SessionMetadata {
89:  return {
90:    sessionId: id,
91:    engineVersion: '0.8.2',
92:    nodeVersion: 'v20.0.0',
93:    recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:00.000Z',
94:    startTick: 0,
95:    endTick: 10,
96:    persistedEndTick: 10,
97:    durationTicks: 10,
98:    sourceKind: 'session',
99:    ...overrides,
100:  };
101:}
102:
103:function snapshot(tick: number): SessionSnapshotEntry {
104:  return {
105:    tick,
106:    snapshot: { tick } as never,
107:  };
108:}
109:
110:function writeBundle(dir: string, meta: SessionMetadata, attachments: AttachmentDescriptor[] = []): void {
111:  const sink = new FileSink(dir);
112:  sink.open(meta);
113:  sink.writeSnapshot(snapshot(meta.startTick));
114:  if (meta.persistedEndTick !== meta.startTick) {
115:    sink.writeSnapshot(snapshot(meta.persistedEndTick));
116:  }
117:  for (const attachment of attachments) {
118:    sink.writeAttachment(attachment, new Uint8Array([1, 2, 3]));
119:  }
120:  sink.close();
121:}
122:
123:function writeInvalidManifest(dir: string, manifest: unknown): void {
124:  mkdirSync(dir, { recursive: true });
125:  writeFileSync(join(dir, 'manifest.json'), JSON.stringify(manifest, null, 2));
126:}
127:
128:function expectCorpusError(fn: () => unknown, code: string): CorpusIndexError {
129:  try {
130:    fn();
131:  } catch (error) {
132:    expect(error).toBeInstanceOf(CorpusIndexError);
133:    expect(error).toBeInstanceOf(SessionRecordingError);
134:    expect((error as CorpusIndexError).details.code).toBe(code);
135:    return error as CorpusIndexError;
136:  }
137:  throw new Error(`expected CorpusIndexError ${code}`);
138:}
139:```

141:- [ ] Add discovery, ordering, and immutable-entry tests.
142:
143:```ts
144:describe('BundleCorpus discovery and entries', () => {
145:  it('indexes a root bundle with key "." and freezes entry metadata', () => {
146:    const root = tempRoot();
147:    writeBundle(root, metadata('root', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:01.000Z' }));
148:
149:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root, { scanDepth: 'root' });
150:    const entries = corpus.entries();
151:
152:    expect(entries.map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['.']);
153:    expect(entries[0].dir).toBe(root);
154:    expect(Object.isFrozen(entries[0])).toBe(true);
155:    expect(Object.isFrozen(entries[0].metadata)).toBe(true);
156:    expect(corpus.get('.')).toBe(entries[0]);
157:
158:    expect(() => {
159:      (entries[0].metadata as SessionMetadata).sessionId = 'mutated';
160:    }).toThrow(TypeError);
161:    expect(corpus.entries()[0].metadata.sessionId).toBe('root');
162:  });
163:
164:  it('honors scanDepth and sorts by recordedAt, sessionId, then key', () => {
165:    const root = tempRoot();
166:    writeBundle(join(root, 'b'), metadata('s-2', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:02.000Z' }));
167:    writeBundle(join(root, 'a'), metadata('s-1', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:02.000Z' }));
168:    writeBundle(join(root, 'nested', 'c'), metadata('s-0', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:00.000Z' }));
169:
170:    expect(new BundleCorpus(root, { scanDepth: 'root' }).entries()).toEqual([]);
171:    expect(new BundleCorpus(root, { scanDepth: 'children' }).entries().map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['a', 'b']);
172:    expect(new BundleCorpus(root, { scanDepth: 'all' }).entries().map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['nested/c', 'a', 'b']);
173:  });
174:
175:  it('stops descending once a directory is a bundle', () => {
176:    const root = tempRoot();
177:    writeBundle(join(root, 'outer'), metadata('outer'));
178:    writeBundle(join(root, 'outer', 'nested'), metadata('nested'));
179:
180:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
181:    expect(corpus.entries().map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['outer']);
182:  });
183:
184:  it('uses locale-independent code-unit ordering for ties', () => {
185:    const root = tempRoot();
186:    writeBundle(join(root, 'lower'), metadata('alpha', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:01.000Z' }));
187:    writeBundle(join(root, 'upper'), metadata('Zulu', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:01.000Z' }));
188:
189:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
190:    expect(corpus.entries().map((entry) => entry.metadata.sessionId)).toEqual(['Zulu', 'alpha']);
191:  });
192:
193:  it('skips symlinked directories when the platform permits creating them', () => {
194:    const root = tempRoot();
195:    const target = join(root, 'target');
196:    writeBundle(target, metadata('target'));
197:    try {
198:      symlinkSync(target, join(root, 'link'), 'junction');
199:    } catch {
200:      return;
201:    }
202:
203:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
204:    expect(corpus.entries().map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['target']);
205:  });
206:});
207:```

209:- [ ] Add manifest-only, sidecar, query, missing-key, invalid-manifest, FileSink, and metrics tests.
210:
211:```ts
212:describe('BundleCorpus query and loading contracts', () => {
213:  it('lists from manifest without reading malformed streams until loadBundle', () => {
214:    const root = tempRoot();
215:    const dir = join(root, 'bad-stream');
216:    writeBundle(dir, metadata('bad-stream'));
217:    writeFileSync(join(dir, 'ticks.jsonl'), '{"tick":\n{}\n');
218:
219:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
220:    expect(corpus.entries().map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['bad-stream']);
221:    expect(() => corpus.loadBundle('bad-stream')).toThrow();
222:  });
223:
224:  it('does not read missing sidecar bytes during listing or loadBundle', () => {
225:    const root = tempRoot();
226:    const dir = join(root, 'sidecar');
227:    writeBundle(dir, metadata('sidecar'), [
228:      { id: 'screen', mime: 'image/png', sizeBytes: 3, ref: { sidecar: true } },
229:    ]);
230:    rmSync(join(dir, 'attachments', 'screen.png'));
231:
232:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
233:    const entry = corpus.entries({ attachmentMime: 'image/png' })[0];
234:    expect(entry.attachmentCount).toBe(1);
235:    expect(entry.attachmentBytes).toBe(3);
236:    expect(entry.attachmentMimes).toEqual(['image/png']);
237:    expect(entry.loadBundle().attachments).toHaveLength(1);
238:    expect(() => entry.openSource().readSidecar('screen')).toThrow();
239:  });
240:
241:  it('loads bundles lazily one iterator step at a time', () => {
242:    const root = tempRoot();
243:    writeBundle(join(root, 'first'), metadata('first', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:01.000Z' }));
244:    const second = join(root, 'second');
245:    writeBundle(second, metadata('second', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:02.000Z' }));
246:    writeFileSync(join(second, 'ticks.jsonl'), '{"tick":\n{}\n');
247:
248:    const iterator = new BundleCorpus(root).bundles();
249:    const first = iterator.next();
250:    expect(first.done).toBe(false);
251:    expect(first.value.metadata.sessionId).toBe('first');
252:    expect(() => iterator.next()).toThrow();
253:  });
254:
255:  it('matches attachmentMime when any MIME overlaps the requested set', () => {
256:    const root = tempRoot();
257:    writeBundle(join(root, 'mixed'), metadata('mixed'), [
258:      { id: 'screen', mime: 'image/png', sizeBytes: 3, ref: { sidecar: true } },
259:      { id: 'trace', mime: 'application/json', sizeBytes: 3, ref: { sidecar: true } },
260:    ]);
261:
262:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
263:    expect(corpus.get('mixed')?.attachmentMimes).toEqual(['application/json', 'image/png']);
264:    expect(corpus.entries({ attachmentMime: 'application/json' }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['mixed']);
265:    expect(corpus.entries({ attachmentMime: ['text/plain', 'image/png'] }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['mixed']);
266:    expect(corpus.entries({ attachmentMime: ['text/plain', 'text/csv'] }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual([]);
267:  });
268:
269:  it('filters by manifest fields and ANDs query fields', () => {
270:    const root = tempRoot();
271:    writeBundle(join(root, 'seeded'), metadata('seeded', {
272:      recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:01.000Z',
273:      sourceKind: 'synthetic',
274:      sourceLabel: 'random',
275:      policySeed: 42,
276:      durationTicks: 30,
277:      endTick: 30,
278:      persistedEndTick: 30,
279:    }));
280:    writeBundle(join(root, 'unseeded'), metadata('unseeded', {
281:      recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:02.000Z',
282:      sourceKind: 'synthetic',
283:      durationTicks: 5,
284:      endTick: 5,
285:      persistedEndTick: 5,
286:    }));
287:
288:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
289:    expect(corpus.entries({ sourceKind: 'synthetic', policySeed: { min: 40, max: 50 } }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['seeded']);
290:    expect(corpus.entries({ sourceLabel: 'random' }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['seeded']);
291:    expect(corpus.entries({ durationTicks: { min: 10 }, recordedAt: { from: '2026-04-27T00:00:00.000Z', to: '2026-04-27T00:00:01.000Z' } }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['seeded']);
292:    expect(corpus.entries({ key: /seed/ }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['seeded', 'unseeded']);
293:    const stateful = /seed/g;
294:    expect(corpus.entries({ key: stateful }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['seeded', 'unseeded']);
295:    expect(stateful.lastIndex).toBe(0);
296:  });
297:
298:  it('derives failure counts and materializedEndTick from metadata', () => {
299:    const root = tempRoot();
300:    writeBundle(join(root, 'complete'), metadata('complete', { endTick: 20, persistedEndTick: 20, durationTicks: 20 }));
301:    writeBundle(join(root, 'incomplete'), metadata('incomplete', {
302:      incomplete: true,
303:      endTick: 50,
304:      persistedEndTick: 25,
305:      durationTicks: 50,
306:      failedTicks: [26, 27],
307:    }));
308:
309:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
310:    expect(corpus.get('complete')?.materializedEndTick).toBe(20);
311:    expect(corpus.get('incomplete')?.materializedEndTick).toBe(25);
312:    expect(corpus.entries({ incomplete: true }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['incomplete']);
313:    expect(corpus.entries({ incomplete: false }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['complete']);
314:    expect(corpus.entries({ materializedEndTick: { max: 25 }, failedTickCount: { min: 1 } }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['incomplete']);
315:    expect(corpus.entries({ endTick: { min: 50 } }).map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['incomplete']);
316:    const failedTicks = corpus.get('incomplete')!.metadata.failedTicks!;
317:    expect(Object.isFrozen(failedTicks)).toBe(true);
318:    expect(() => failedTicks.push(99)).toThrow(TypeError);
319:    expect(corpus.get('incomplete')!.metadata.failedTicks).toEqual([26, 27]);
320:  });
321:
322:  it('rejects invalid query ranges and non-canonical recordedAt bounds', () => {
323:    const root = tempRoot();
324:    writeBundle(join(root, 'bundle'), metadata('bundle'));
325:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
326:
327:    expectCorpusError(() => corpus.entries({ durationTicks: { min: 10, max: 1 } }), 'query_invalid');
328:    expectCorpusError(() => corpus.entries({ startTick: { min: 0.5 } }), 'query_invalid');
329:    expectCorpusError(() => corpus.entries({ policySeed: Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY }), 'query_invalid');
330:    expectCorpusError(() => corpus.entries({ recordedAt: { from: '2026-04-27' } }), 'query_invalid');
331:  });
332:
333:  it('returns undefined for get and throws entry_missing for strict missing-key APIs', () => {
334:    const root = tempRoot();
335:    writeBundle(join(root, 'bundle'), metadata('bundle'));
336:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
337:
338:    expect(corpus.get('missing')).toBeUndefined();
339:    expectCorpusError(() => corpus.openSource('missing'), 'entry_missing');
340:    expectCorpusError(() => corpus.loadBundle('missing'), 'entry_missing');
341:  });
342:
343:  it('handles invalid manifests strictly or through skipInvalid diagnostics', () => {
344:    const root = tempRoot();
345:    writeBundle(join(root, 'good'), metadata('good'));
346:    writeInvalidManifest(join(root, 'bad'), {
347:      schemaVersion: 1,
348:      metadata: metadata('bad', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:00-07:00' }),
349:      attachments: [],
350:    });
351:
352:    expectCorpusError(() => new BundleCorpus(root), 'manifest_invalid');
353:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root, { skipInvalid: true });
354:    expect(corpus.entries().map((entry) => entry.key)).toEqual(['good']);
355:    expect(corpus.invalidEntries).toHaveLength(1);
356:    expect(corpus.invalidEntries[0].error.details.code).toBe('manifest_invalid');
357:  });
358:
359:  it('loads FileSink bundles lazily and composes with runMetrics', () => {
360:    const root = tempRoot();
361:    writeBundle(join(root, 'one'), metadata('one', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:01.000Z' }));
362:    writeBundle(join(root, 'two'), metadata('two', { recordedAt: '2026-04-27T00:00:02.000Z', sourceKind: 'synthetic' }));
363:
364:    const corpus = new BundleCorpus(root);
365:    expect(corpus.openSource('one').readSnapshot(0)).toEqual(snapshot(0).snapshot);
366:    expect(corpus.loadBundle('one')).toEqual(new FileSink(join(root, 'one')).toBundle());
367:    expect([...corpus].map((bundle) => bundle.metadata.sessionId)).toEqual(['one', 'two']);
368:    expect(runMetrics(corpus.bundles({ sourceKind: 'synthetic' }), [bundleCount()]).bundleCount).toBe(1);
369:  });
370:});

376:### Step 2: Implement `src/bundle-corpus.ts`
377:
378:- [ ] Create `src/bundle-corpus.ts` with the public API and helpers below. Keep the module self-contained; do not modify FileSink, SessionSource, SessionBundle, SessionReplayer, or runMetrics.
379:
380:```ts
381:import { existsSync, lstatSync, readdirSync, readFileSync, realpathSync } from 'node:fs';
382:import { join, relative, resolve, sep } from 'node:path';
383:import type { JsonValue } from './json.js';
384:import type { AttachmentDescriptor, SessionBundle, SessionMetadata } from './session-bundle.js';
385:import { SESSION_BUNDLE_SCHEMA_VERSION } from './session-bundle.js';
386:import { SessionRecordingError } from './session-errors.js';
387:import { FileSink } from './session-file-sink.js';
388:import type { SessionSource } from './session-sink.js';
389:
390:const MANIFEST_FILE = 'manifest.json';
391:
392:export type BundleCorpusScanDepth = 'root' | 'children' | 'all';
393:
394:export interface BundleCorpusOptions {
395:  scanDepth?: BundleCorpusScanDepth;
396:  skipInvalid?: boolean;
397:}
398:
399:export interface NumberRange {
400:  min?: number;
401:  max?: number;
402:}
403:
404:export interface IsoTimeRange {
405:  from?: string;
406:  to?: string;
407:}
408:
409:export type OneOrMany<T> = T | readonly T[];
410:
411:export interface BundleQuery {
412:  key?: string | RegExp;
413:  sessionId?: OneOrMany<string>;
414:  sourceKind?: OneOrMany<SessionMetadata['sourceKind']>;
415:  sourceLabel?: OneOrMany<string>;
416:  engineVersion?: OneOrMany<string>;
417:  nodeVersion?: OneOrMany<string>;
418:  incomplete?: boolean;
419:  durationTicks?: NumberRange;
420:  startTick?: NumberRange;
421:  endTick?: NumberRange;
422:  persistedEndTick?: NumberRange;
423:  materializedEndTick?: NumberRange;
424:  failedTickCount?: NumberRange;
425:  policySeed?: number | NumberRange;
426:  recordedAt?: IsoTimeRange;
427:  attachmentMime?: OneOrMany<string>;
428:}
429:
430:export type CorpusIndexErrorCode =
431:  | 'root_missing'
432:  | 'manifest_parse'
433:  | 'manifest_invalid'
434:  | 'schema_unsupported'
435:  | 'duplicate_key'
436:  | 'query_invalid'
437:  | 'entry_missing';
438:
439:export interface CorpusIndexErrorDetails {
440:  readonly [key: string]: JsonValue;
441:  readonly code: CorpusIndexErrorCode;
442:  readonly path: string | null;
443:  readonly key: string | null;
444:  readonly message: string | null;
445:}
446:
447:export class CorpusIndexError extends SessionRecordingError {
448:  override readonly details: CorpusIndexErrorDetails;
449:
450:  constructor(message: string, details: CorpusIndexErrorDetails) {
451:    super(message, details);
452:    this.name = 'CorpusIndexError';
453:    this.details = details;
454:  }
455:}
456:
457:export interface InvalidCorpusEntry {
458:  readonly path: string;
459:  readonly error: CorpusIndexError;
460:}
461:
462:export interface BundleCorpusEntry {
463:  readonly key: string;
464:  readonly dir: string;
465:  readonly schemaVersion: typeof SESSION_BUNDLE_SCHEMA_VERSION;
466:  readonly metadata: Readonly<SessionMetadata>;
467:  readonly attachmentCount: number;
468:  readonly attachmentBytes: number;
469:  readonly attachmentMimes: readonly string[];
470:  readonly hasFailures: boolean;
471:  readonly failedTickCount: number;
472:  readonly materializedEndTick: number;
473:  openSource(): SessionSource;
474:  loadBundle<
475:    TEventMap extends Record<keyof TEventMap, unknown> = Record<string, never>,
476:    TCommandMap extends Record<keyof TCommandMap, unknown> = Record<string, never>,
477:    TDebug = JsonValue,
478:  >(): SessionBundle<TEventMap, TCommandMap, TDebug>;
479:}
480:```
481:
482:- [ ] Add implementation helpers in the same file with these exact responsibilities:
483:
484:```ts
485:interface FileManifest {
486:  schemaVersion: typeof SESSION_BUNDLE_SCHEMA_VERSION;
487:  metadata: SessionMetadata;
488:  attachments: AttachmentDescriptor[];
489:}
490:
491:interface CorpusIndexErrorDetailsInput {
492:  readonly [key: string]: JsonValue | undefined;
493:  readonly code: CorpusIndexErrorCode;
494:  readonly path?: string;
495:  readonly key?: string;
496:  readonly message?: string;
497:}
498:
499:function normalizeDetails(input: CorpusIndexErrorDetailsInput): CorpusIndexErrorDetails {
500:  const details: Record<string, JsonValue> = {};
501:  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(input)) {
502:    if (value !== undefined) details[key] = value;
503:  }
504:  details.code = input.code;
505:  details.path = input.path ?? null;
506:  details.key = input.key ?? null;
507:  details.message = input.message ?? null;
508:  return Object.freeze(details) as CorpusIndexErrorDetails;
509:}
510:
511:function corpusError(message: string, details: CorpusIndexErrorDetailsInput): CorpusIndexError {
512:  return new CorpusIndexError(message, normalizeDetails(details));
513:}
514:
515:function isRecord(value: unknown): value is Record<string, unknown> {
516:  return typeof value === 'object' && value !== null && !Array.isArray(value);
517:}
518:
519:function assertCanonicalIso(value: unknown, label: string, path: string): string {
520:  if (typeof value !== 'string' || !value.endsWith('Z')) {
521:    throw corpusError(`${label} must be a normalized UTC ISO string`, { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: label });
522:  }
523:  const parsed = new Date(value);
524:  if (!Number.isFinite(parsed.getTime()) || parsed.toISOString() !== value) {
525:    throw corpusError(`${label} must round-trip through Date.toISOString()`, { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: label });
526:  }
527:  return value;
528:}
529:
530:function validateQueryIso(value: unknown, label: string): string {
531:  if (typeof value !== 'string' || !value.endsWith('Z')) {
532:    throw corpusError(`${label} must be a normalized UTC ISO string`, { code: 'query_invalid', message: label });
533:  }
534:  const parsed = new Date(value);
535:  if (!Number.isFinite(parsed.getTime()) || parsed.toISOString() !== value) {
536:    throw corpusError(`${label} must round-trip through Date.toISOString()`, { code: 'query_invalid', message: label });
537:  }
538:  return value;
539:}
540:
541:function assertString(value: unknown, label: string, path: string): string {
542:  if (typeof value !== 'string') {
543:    throw corpusError(`${label} must be a string`, { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: label });
544:  }
545:  return value;
546:}
547:
548:function assertInteger(value: unknown, label: string, path: string): number {
549:  if (typeof value !== 'number' || !Number.isFinite(value) || !Number.isInteger(value)) {
550:    throw corpusError(`${label} must be a finite integer`, { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: label });
551:  }
552:  return value;
553:}
554:```
555:
556:- [ ] Validate manifests with runtime checks instead of trusting JSON casts.
557:
558:```ts
559:function validateMetadata(value: unknown, path: string): SessionMetadata {
560:  if (!isRecord(value)) {
561:    throw corpusError('manifest metadata must be an object', { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: 'metadata' });
562:  }
563:  const sourceKind = value.sourceKind;
564:  if (sourceKind !== 'session' && sourceKind !== 'scenario' && sourceKind !== 'synthetic') {
565:    throw corpusError('metadata.sourceKind must be session, scenario, or synthetic', { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: 'sourceKind' });
566:  }
567:  const failedTicks = value.failedTicks === undefined
568:    ? undefined
569:    : Array.isArray(value.failedTicks)
570:      ? value.failedTicks.map((tick, index) => assertInteger(tick, `failedTicks[${index}]`, path))
571:      : (() => { throw corpusError('metadata.failedTicks must be an array', { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: 'failedTicks' }); })();
572:  const metadata: SessionMetadata = {
573:    sessionId: assertString(value.sessionId, 'sessionId', path),
574:    engineVersion: assertString(value.engineVersion, 'engineVersion', path),
575:    nodeVersion: assertString(value.nodeVersion, 'nodeVersion', path),
576:    recordedAt: assertCanonicalIso(value.recordedAt, 'recordedAt', path),
577:    startTick: assertInteger(value.startTick, 'startTick', path),
578:    endTick: assertInteger(value.endTick, 'endTick', path),
579:    persistedEndTick: assertInteger(value.persistedEndTick, 'persistedEndTick', path),
580:    durationTicks: assertInteger(value.durationTicks, 'durationTicks', path),
581:    sourceKind,
582:  };
583:  if (value.sourceLabel !== undefined) metadata.sourceLabel = assertString(value.sourceLabel, 'sourceLabel', path);
584:  if (value.incomplete !== undefined) {
585:    if (value.incomplete !== true) {
586:      throw corpusError('metadata.incomplete must be true when present', { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: 'incomplete' });
587:    }
588:    metadata.incomplete = true;
589:  }
590:  if (failedTicks) metadata.failedTicks = failedTicks;
591:  if (value.policySeed !== undefined) metadata.policySeed = assertInteger(value.policySeed, 'policySeed', path);
592:  return metadata;
593:}
594:
595:function validateAttachment(value: unknown, path: string, index: number): AttachmentDescriptor {
596:  if (!isRecord(value)) {
597:    throw corpusError(`attachments[${index}] must be an object`, { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: `attachments[${index}]` });
598:  }
599:  const ref = value.ref;
600:  if (!isRecord(ref)) {
601:    throw corpusError(`attachments[${index}].ref must be an object`, { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: `attachments[${index}].ref` });
602:  }
603:  const refKeys = Object.keys(ref).filter((key) => ref[key] !== undefined);
604:  const validRef =
605:    (refKeys.length === 1 && typeof ref.dataUrl === 'string') ||
606:    (refKeys.length === 1 && ref.sidecar === true) ||
607:    (refKeys.length === 1 && ref.auto === true);
608:  if (!validRef) {
609:    throw corpusError(`attachments[${index}].ref must be dataUrl, sidecar, or auto`, { code: 'manifest_invalid', path, message: `attachments[${index}].ref` });
610:  }
611:  return {
612:    id: assertString(value.id, `attachments[${index}].id`, path),
613:    mime: assertString(value.mime, `attachments[${index}].mime`, path),
614:    sizeBytes: assertInteger(value.sizeBytes, `attachments[${index}].sizeBytes`, path),
615:    ref: ref as AttachmentDescriptor['ref'],
616:  };
617:}
618:
619:function readManifest(manifestPath: string): FileManifest {
620:  let parsed: unknown;
621:  try {
622:    parsed = JSON.parse(readFileSync(manifestPath, 'utf-8')) as unknown;
623:  } catch (error) {
624:    throw corpusError(`manifest parse failed: ${(error as Error).message}`, { code: 'manifest_parse', path: manifestPath, message: (error as Error).message });
625:  }
626:  if (!isRecord(parsed)) {
627:    throw corpusError('manifest must be an object', { code: 'manifest_invalid', path: manifestPath, message: 'manifest' });
628:  }
629:  if (parsed.schemaVersion !== SESSION_BUNDLE_SCHEMA_VERSION) {
630:    throw corpusError('unsupported bundle schema version', { code: 'schema_unsupported', path: manifestPath, message: String(parsed.schemaVersion) });
631:  }
632:  if (!Array.isArray(parsed.attachments)) {
633:    throw corpusError('manifest attachments must be an array', { code: 'manifest_invalid', path: manifestPath, message: 'attachments' });
634:  }
635:  return {
636:    schemaVersion: SESSION_BUNDLE_SCHEMA_VERSION,
637:    metadata: validateMetadata(parsed.metadata, manifestPath),
638:    attachments: parsed.attachments.map((attachment, index) => validateAttachment(attachment, manifestPath, index)),
639:  };
640:}
641:```
642:
643:- [ ] Add a locale-independent string comparator. Use it everywhere the corpus exposes deterministic ordering.
644:
645:```ts
646:function compareCodeUnit(a: string, b: string): number {
647:  return a < b ? -1 : a > b ? 1 : 0;
648:}
649:```

651:- [ ] Add `BundleCorpus` with synchronous construction, deterministic discovery, immutable entries, query filtering, and lazy bundle iteration.
652:
653:```ts
654:export class BundleCorpus implements Iterable<SessionBundle> {
655:  readonly rootDir: string;
656:  readonly invalidEntries: readonly InvalidCorpusEntry[];
657:  private readonly _entries: readonly BundleCorpusEntry[];
658:  private readonly _byKey: ReadonlyMap<string, BundleCorpusEntry>;
659:
660:  constructor(rootDir: string, options: BundleCorpusOptions = {}) {
661:    const root = resolve(rootDir);
662:    if (!existsSync(root) || !lstatSync(root).isDirectory()) {
663:      throw corpusError('corpus root is missing or is not a directory', { code: 'root_missing', path: root });
664:    }
665:    this.rootDir = realpathSync(root);
666:    const invalidEntries: InvalidCorpusEntry[] = [];
667:    const found = discoverBundleDirs(this.rootDir, options.scanDepth ?? 'all');
668:    const byKey = new Map<string, BundleCorpusEntry>();
669:    const entries: BundleCorpusEntry[] = [];
670:
671:    for (const dir of found) {
672:      const key = keyForDir(this.rootDir, dir);
673:      if (byKey.has(key)) {
674:        throw corpusError(`duplicate corpus key ${key}`, { code: 'duplicate_key', path: dir, key });
675:      }
676:      try {
677:        const entry = makeEntry(dir, key, readManifest(join(dir, MANIFEST_FILE)));
678:        byKey.set(key, entry);
679:        entries.push(entry);
680:      } catch (error) {
681:        if (options.skipInvalid && error instanceof CorpusIndexError && error.details.code !== 'duplicate_key') {
682:          invalidEntries.push(Object.freeze({ path: join(dir, MANIFEST_FILE), error }));
683:          continue;
684:        }
685:        throw error;
686:      }
687:    }
688:
689:    entries.sort(compareEntries);
690:    this._entries = Object.freeze(entries.slice());
691:    this._byKey = new Map(entries.map((entry) => [entry.key, entry]));
692:    this.invalidEntries = Object.freeze(invalidEntries.slice());
693:  }
694:
695:  entries(query?: BundleQuery): readonly BundleCorpusEntry[] {
696:    const predicate = query ? compileQuery(query) : () => true;
697:    return Object.freeze(this._entries.filter(predicate));
698:  }
699:
700:  *bundles(query?: BundleQuery): IterableIterator<SessionBundle> {
701:    for (const entry of this.entries(query)) {
702:      yield entry.loadBundle();
703:    }
704:  }
705:
706:  get(key: string): BundleCorpusEntry | undefined {
707:    return this._byKey.get(key);
708:  }
709:
710:  openSource(key: string): SessionSource {
711:    return requireEntry(this._byKey, key).openSource();
712:  }
713:
714:  loadBundle<
715:    TEventMap extends Record<keyof TEventMap, unknown> = Record<string, never>,
716:    TCommandMap extends Record<keyof TCommandMap, unknown> = Record<string, never>,
717:    TDebug = JsonValue,
718:  >(key: string): SessionBundle<TEventMap, TCommandMap, TDebug> {
719:    return requireEntry(this._byKey, key).loadBundle<TEventMap, TCommandMap, TDebug>();
720:  }
721:
722:  [Symbol.iterator](): IterableIterator<SessionBundle> {
723:    return this.bundles();
724:  }
725:}
726:```
727:
728:- [ ] Implement the remaining private helpers exactly enough to satisfy the tests and design:
729:
730:```ts
731:function discoverBundleDirs(root: string, depth: BundleCorpusScanDepth): string[] {
732:  const out: string[] = [];
733:  function visit(dir: string, remaining: number | 'all'): void {
734:    if (existsSync(join(dir, MANIFEST_FILE))) {
735:      out.push(dir);
736:      return;
737:    }
738:    if (remaining === 0) return;
739:    const nextRemaining = remaining === 'all' ? 'all' : remaining - 1;
740:    const children = readdirSync(dir, { withFileTypes: true })
741:      .filter((dirent) => dirent.isDirectory() && !dirent.isSymbolicLink())
742:      .map((dirent) => dirent.name)
743:      .sort(compareCodeUnit);
744:    for (const child of children) visit(join(dir, child), nextRemaining);
745:  }
746:  visit(root, depth === 'root' ? 0 : depth === 'children' ? 1 : 'all');
747:  return out;
748:}
749:
750:function keyForDir(root: string, dir: string): string {
751:  const rel = relative(root, dir);
752:  if (rel.length === 0) return '.';
753:  return rel.split(sep).join('/');
754:}
755:
756:function makeEntry(dir: string, key: string, manifest: FileManifest): BundleCorpusEntry {
757:  const frozenFailedTicks = manifest.metadata.failedTicks ? Object.freeze(manifest.metadata.failedTicks.slice()) : undefined;
758:  const metadata: Readonly<SessionMetadata> = Object.freeze({
759:    ...manifest.metadata,
760:    ...(frozenFailedTicks ? { failedTicks: frozenFailedTicks as number[] } : {}),
761:  });
762:  const attachmentMimes = Object.freeze([...new Set(manifest.attachments.map((attachment) => attachment.mime))].sort(compareCodeUnit));
763:  const materializedEndTick = metadata.incomplete === true ? metadata.persistedEndTick : metadata.endTick;
764:  const entry: BundleCorpusEntry = {
765:    key,
766:    dir,
767:    schemaVersion: manifest.schemaVersion,
768:    metadata,
769:    attachmentCount: manifest.attachments.length,
770:    attachmentBytes: manifest.attachments.reduce((sum, attachment) => sum + attachment.sizeBytes, 0),
771:    attachmentMimes,
772:    hasFailures: (metadata.failedTicks?.length ?? 0) > 0,
773:    failedTickCount: metadata.failedTicks?.length ?? 0,
774:    materializedEndTick,
775:    openSource: () => new FileSink(dir),
776:    loadBundle: <
777:      TEventMap extends Record<keyof TEventMap, unknown> = Record<string, never>,
778:      TCommandMap extends Record<keyof TCommandMap, unknown> = Record<string, never>,
779:      TDebug = JsonValue,
780:    >() => new FileSink(dir).toBundle() as SessionBundle<TEventMap, TCommandMap, TDebug>,
781:  };
782:  return Object.freeze(entry);
783:}
784:
785:function compareEntries(a: BundleCorpusEntry, b: BundleCorpusEntry): number {
786:  return compareCodeUnit(a.metadata.recordedAt, b.metadata.recordedAt)
787:    || compareCodeUnit(a.metadata.sessionId, b.metadata.sessionId)
788:    || compareCodeUnit(a.key, b.key);
789:}
790:
791:function requireEntry(map: ReadonlyMap<string, BundleCorpusEntry>, key: string): BundleCorpusEntry {
792:  const entry = map.get(key);
793:  if (!entry) {
794:    throw corpusError(`corpus entry ${key} not found`, { code: 'entry_missing', key });
795:  }
796:  return entry;
797:}
798:```
