800:- [ ] Implement `compileQuery(query)` with inclusive numeric ranges, one-or-many matching, optional-field exclusion, `attachmentMime` any-match, canonical `recordedAt` bounds, and AND semantics.
801:
802:```ts
803:function asArray<T>(value: OneOrMany<T>): readonly T[] {
804:  return Array.isArray(value) ? value : [value];
805:}
806:
807:function assertQueryInteger(value: unknown, label: string): number {
808:  if (typeof value !== 'number' || !Number.isFinite(value) || !Number.isInteger(value)) {
809:    throw corpusError(`${label} must be a finite integer`, { code: 'query_invalid', message: label });
810:  }
811:  return value;
812:}
813:
814:function assertNumberRange(range: NumberRange, label: string): Required<NumberRange> {
815:  if (range.min !== undefined) assertQueryInteger(range.min, `${label}.min`);
816:  if (range.max !== undefined) assertQueryInteger(range.max, `${label}.max`);
817:  const min = range.min ?? Number.NEGATIVE_INFINITY;
818:  const max = range.max ?? Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY;
819:  if (min > max) {
820:    throw corpusError(`${label}.min must be <= max`, { code: 'query_invalid', message: label });
821:  }
822:  return { min, max };
823:}
824:
825:function matchesRange(value: number, range: Required<NumberRange>): boolean {
826:  return value >= range.min && value <= range.max;
827:}
828:
829:function matchesOne<T>(value: T | undefined, expected: OneOrMany<T> | undefined): boolean {
830:  if (expected === undefined) return true;
831:  if (value === undefined) return false;
832:  return asArray(expected).includes(value);
833:}
834:
835:function matchesKey(value: string, expected: string | RegExp | undefined): boolean {
836:  if (expected === undefined) return true;
837:  if (typeof expected === 'string') return value === expected;
838:  expected.lastIndex = 0;
839:  const matched = expected.test(value);
840:  expected.lastIndex = 0;
841:  return matched;
842:}
843:
844:function compileQuery(query: BundleQuery): (entry: BundleCorpusEntry) => boolean {
845:  const ranges = {
846:    durationTicks: query.durationTicks ? assertNumberRange(query.durationTicks, 'durationTicks') : undefined,
847:    startTick: query.startTick ? assertNumberRange(query.startTick, 'startTick') : undefined,
848:    endTick: query.endTick ? assertNumberRange(query.endTick, 'endTick') : undefined,
849:    persistedEndTick: query.persistedEndTick ? assertNumberRange(query.persistedEndTick, 'persistedEndTick') : undefined,
850:    materializedEndTick: query.materializedEndTick ? assertNumberRange(query.materializedEndTick, 'materializedEndTick') : undefined,
851:    failedTickCount: query.failedTickCount ? assertNumberRange(query.failedTickCount, 'failedTickCount') : undefined,
852:    policySeed: typeof query.policySeed === 'object' ? assertNumberRange(query.policySeed, 'policySeed') : undefined,
853:  };
854:  const policySeedScalar = typeof query.policySeed === 'number' ? assertQueryInteger(query.policySeed, 'policySeed') : undefined;
855:  const recordedAtFrom = query.recordedAt?.from === undefined ? undefined : validateQueryIso(query.recordedAt.from, 'recordedAt.from');
856:  const recordedAtTo = query.recordedAt?.to === undefined ? undefined : validateQueryIso(query.recordedAt.to, 'recordedAt.to');
857:  if (recordedAtFrom && recordedAtTo && recordedAtFrom > recordedAtTo) {
858:    throw corpusError('recordedAt.from must be <= recordedAt.to', { code: 'query_invalid', message: 'recordedAt' });
859:  }
860:
861:  return (entry) => {
862:    const m = entry.metadata;
863:    if (!matchesKey(entry.key, query.key)) return false;
864:    if (!matchesOne(m.sessionId, query.sessionId)) return false;
865:    if (!matchesOne(m.sourceKind, query.sourceKind)) return false;
866:    if (!matchesOne(m.sourceLabel, query.sourceLabel)) return false;
867:    if (!matchesOne(m.engineVersion, query.engineVersion)) return false;
868:    if (!matchesOne(m.nodeVersion, query.nodeVersion)) return false;
869:    if (query.incomplete !== undefined && (m.incomplete === true) !== query.incomplete) return false;
870:    if (ranges.durationTicks && !matchesRange(m.durationTicks, ranges.durationTicks)) return false;
871:    if (ranges.startTick && !matchesRange(m.startTick, ranges.startTick)) return false;
872:    if (ranges.endTick && !matchesRange(m.endTick, ranges.endTick)) return false;
873:    if (ranges.persistedEndTick && !matchesRange(m.persistedEndTick, ranges.persistedEndTick)) return false;
874:    if (ranges.materializedEndTick && !matchesRange(entry.materializedEndTick, ranges.materializedEndTick)) return false;
875:    if (ranges.failedTickCount && !matchesRange(entry.failedTickCount, ranges.failedTickCount)) return false;
876:    if (policySeedScalar !== undefined && m.policySeed !== policySeedScalar) return false;
877:    if (ranges.policySeed && (m.policySeed === undefined || !matchesRange(m.policySeed, ranges.policySeed))) return false;
878:    if (recordedAtFrom && m.recordedAt < recordedAtFrom) return false;
879:    if (recordedAtTo && m.recordedAt > recordedAtTo) return false;
880:    if (query.attachmentMime && !entry.attachmentMimes.some((mime) => asArray(query.attachmentMime!).includes(mime))) return false;
881:    return true;
882:  };
883:}
884:```

1067:## Acceptance Checklist
1068:
1069:- [ ] Public exports include `BundleCorpus`, `BundleCorpusScanDepth`, `BundleCorpusOptions`, `BundleCorpusEntry`, `BundleQuery`, `OneOrMany`, `NumberRange`, `IsoTimeRange`, `CorpusIndexError`, `CorpusIndexErrorCode`, `CorpusIndexErrorDetails`, and `InvalidCorpusEntry`.
1070:- [ ] Construction discovers root, child, and nested FileSink bundle directories according to `scanDepth`; root bundle key is `'.'`; descendant keys use `/`.
1071:- [ ] Discovery skips symlinked directories and stops descending inside bundle directories.
1072:- [ ] `entries(query?)` reads manifests only and returns deterministic frozen entries in `recordedAt`, `sessionId`, `key` order.
1073:- [ ] `bundles(query?)` and `[Symbol.iterator]` lazily load full bundles through FileSink.
1074:- [ ] `get` returns `undefined` for missing keys; `openSource` and `loadBundle` throw `CorpusIndexError` with `details.code === 'entry_missing'`.
1075:- [ ] Query filters cover exact, one-or-many, numeric range, ISO range, optional field, failure count, materialized end tick, key RegExp, and attachment MIME any-match semantics.
1076:- [ ] Invalid query and invalid manifest errors use `CorpusIndexError` with JSON-shaped `details.code`.
1077:- [ ] `skipInvalid` records invalid manifests and omits them from entries.
1078:- [ ] `runMetrics(corpus.bundles(query), metrics)` is covered by tests.
1079:- [ ] Docs, ADRs, roadmap, changelog, devlog, API reference, README badge, and version bump ship in the same commit.

1:## Core rules
2:
3:- Use test-driven development for behavior changes: write or update tests first, then make them pass. Test the contract, not the code: tests should focus primarily on app experience and mechanisms.
4:- For each desired change, make the change easy, then make the easy change.
5:- CRITICAL: Before implementing a change, write a plan and ask Codex and Claude to brainstorm with you and double check. Iterate until opinions converge on approval, just like code review.
6:- Verify every change against this project's gates: `npm test`, `npm run typecheck`, `npm run lint`, `npm run build`. All four must pass before declaring a task done.
7:- **Multi-CLI code review is mandatory for every behavior or code change before declaring the task done.** Run Codex + Claude per the Code review section, synthesize their findings into `docs/reviews/<scope>/<date>/<iteration_number>/REVIEW.md`, address every real finding, and re-review until reviewers nitpick instead of catching real bugs. This applies to all changes ΓÇö single-file fixes, doc-only edits with code implications, refactors, and big features alike. Do not rationalize your way out of review with phrases like "single-file behavior fix," "trivial change," "TDD coverage is sufficient," "subagent dispatch is a tool not a mandate," or any equivalent. The Code review section is non-negotiable; the Team-of-subagents flexibility clause does NOT cover the multi-CLI review step. Skipping review is a process regression and must be corrected by running the review post-hoc on the same branch before merge.
8:- When the change is visual:
9:  - Capture a before screenshot.
10:  - Apply the change.
11:  - Capture an after screenshot.
12:  - Generate a pixel diff and use that as verification alongside the normal test/build gates.
13:
14:## Team of subagents (flexible, not rigid)
15:
16:Subagent dispatch is a tool, not a mandate. Use it when:
17:
18:- Context budget matters (a long-running investigation that would clutter the main thread)
19:- Work is genuinely parallel (independent searches or independent reviews)
20:- A specialist agent type fits naturally (Explore for codebase audits, etc.)
21:
22:For sequential focused work in the main thread, act as engineer directly ΓÇö dispatching adds overhead and removes the ability to course-correct quickly.
23:
24:When you do dispatch, the team roles below describe how to brief them. The Team Lead role is always you (the main agent).
25:
26:- **Team lead** (always the main agent):
27:  - Breaks the human's request into atomic tasks, selects the appropriate domain specialists, routes the tasks, and acts as the final gatekeeper before merging.
28:  - If tests fail or review consensus is not reached after 3 iterations, execute a hard abort. Ask the user before destructive operations like `git reset --hard`. Dump error logs and the failed approach into `docs/learning/lessons.md`, and start over with a fresh plan that explicitly avoids the failed approach.
29:- **Architect**: Acts as a consultant. Drafts the initial implementation plan and verifies it against ARCHITECTURE.md before work dispatches.
30:- **Game designer**: Validates that the game mechanism works well and is fun. Researches local and online sources to ground opinions.
31:- **Software engineer**: Handles code writing.
32:  - CRITICAL: After coding, ask the code reviewer to review (see Code review section).
33:  - Iterate with reviewers ΓÇö diff reviews take ~5 minutes per CLI; use `run_in_background: true` and an `until [ -s <output-file> ]; do sleep 8; done` poller to wait without burning context or hitting harness sleep limits.
34:  - After addressing review comments, ask the reviewer to verify the fix.
35:  - If engineer + reviewer cannot reach consensus after 3 iterations, escalate to the Tie-Breaker.
36:  - Save reviewer feedback under `docs/reviews/<scope>/<date>/<iteration_number>/`, mirroring the full-codebase review convention (see `docs/reviews/full/<date>/<iteration_number>/` for the existing precedent). For per-task diff reviews, `<scope>` is a kebab-case task slug (e.g., `synthetic-playtest-T2`, `behavioral-metrics-T1`); for full-codebase reviews `<scope>` is `full`. Each iteration directory contains:
37:    - `raw/codex.md`, `raw/opus.md` ΓÇö per-CLI raw outputs (Claude's file is `opus.md` to match the existing convention; optional `*.stdout.log` / `*.stderr.log` companions for raw command output)
38:    - `diff.md` ΓÇö the diff being reviewed
39:    - `REVIEW.md` ΓÇö your synthesized summary of the raw outputs with severity-tagged findings
40:  - `<iteration_number>` starts at 1 and increments for each re-review. Re-reviewers should consider previous iterations' `REVIEW.md` + `docs/learning/lessons.md` + the new diff so they verify earlier fixes landed and don't re-flag old issues.
41:  - After folding the final iteration's `REVIEW.md` into the devlog entry for the task, the review directory stays in `docs/reviews/<scope>/<date>/` as a historical artifact (do not delete ΓÇö these are valuable audit trails alongside the full-review history).
42:  - Continue iterating until reviewers nitpick instead of catching real bugs / giving substantial feedback. Do not get stuck in an infinite loop.
43:- **Code reviewer**: Follow the Code review section.
44:- **Tie breaker**: Use `claude --model opus`. Its prompt dictates that it must definitively choose to either ACCEPT the current diff (overriding the reviewer) or REJECT it with a mandatory, prescriptive patch. The Tie-Breaker's decision is final.
45:
46:## Code review (mandatory; not optional)
47:
48:This section is the operational implementation of the Core-rules "Multi-CLI code review is mandatory" rule. Every code or behavior change runs through this loop before merge ΓÇö no exceptions, no carve-outs for "small" or "single-file" changes.
49:
50:- Use Codex / Claude in CLI to independently review every change. Aspects to review:
51:  1. Design ΓÇö easily scales, generalizes, debugs, can be understood and reasoned about, stays lean.
52:  2. Test coverage.
53:  3. Correctness.
54:  4. Clean code, typing, efficiency, memory leaks. No duplicated logic, inconsistent implementations, violation of boundaries. No file > 500 LOC. Prefer composition over inheritance. Clean up dead code. Do not change app mechanics or behavior unless explicitly asked.
55:
56:  Documentation accuracy is covered by the Documentation discipline section's reviewer prompt addendum ΓÇö do not duplicate the rule here.
57:
58:- A baseline prompt is below; **enrich it with task-specific context** for real reviews ΓÇö the change's intent, prior-iteration findings to verify, files to focus on, and an anti-regression checklist. The bare baseline returns generic feedback; useful reviews need the specifics.
59:
60:  > "You are a senior code reviewer. Flag bugs, security issues, and performance concerns. Do NOT modify files or propose patches. Only return findings, explanations, and suggestions in plain text. Only point out an issue if it is real and important. If there is no issue, say so instead of nit-picking."
61:
62:- Codex:
63:  - `git diff [branch] | codex exec --model gpt-5.4 -c model_reasoning_effort=xhigh -c approval_policy=never --sandbox read-only --ephemeral <prompt>`
64:  - On Windows, `--sandbox read-only` blocks PowerShell `Select-String` invocations the model sometimes attempts; the model recovers via direct file reads, so the review still completes.
65:- Claude:
66:  - With diff piped via stdin: `git diff [branch] | claude -p --model opus --effort xhigh --append-system-prompt <prompt> --allowedTools "Read,Bash(git diff *),Bash(git log *),Bash(git show *)"`
67:  - For full-codebase (no diff): pass the prompt as the positional argument: `claude -p "<full prompt>" --model opus --effort xhigh --allowedTools "Read,Glob,Grep,Bash(git diff *),Bash(git log *),Bash(git show *),Bash(wc *),Bash(ls *),Bash(find *)"`. `--append-system-prompt` is unnecessary and the long-prompt-as-stdin form is not needed.
68:- For full-codebase reviews (no diff), drop the `git diff` pipe and let each CLI agentically explore the workspace from its CWD; keep the same model/effort flags.
69:- **Diff reviews take ~5 minutes per CLI on a multi-hundred-line diff.** Run them in parallel with `run_in_background: true`. Wait via a single background `until` poller (`until [ -s codex.txt ] && [ -s claude.txt ]; do sleep 8; done`) so the harness's no-long-sleeps guard doesn't fire and you don't poll repeatedly.
70:- **If a CLI is unreachable** (quota exhaustion, model name rejected by harness), proceed with the remaining reviewer and note the unreachable CLI in the devlog.
71:
72:## Git
73:
74:- **Commit directly to `main`.** This is a solo-developer project; branches add overhead without payoff and block autonomous progress while waiting for merge authorization. Each coherent change lands as its own commit on `main`. The full suite (`npm test`, `npm run typecheck`, `npm run lint`, `npm run build`) must pass before each commit.
75:- When you iterate, only run affected tests.
76:- After confidence in the change, run the full suite to make sure you didn't accidentally break anything before committing.
77:- Commit as soon as you have a coherent, self-contained unit of change.
78:- Commit durable docs you added if you are not planning to remove them.
79:- **No branches needed for normal work.** Branches are reserved for explicit experimentation that you intend to keep isolated from `main` (and even then, prefer revertable single-commit experiments on `main`). The earlier `agent/<task>` branch convention and the merge-authorization gate are removed ΓÇö they were artifacts of a multi-developer workflow that doesn't apply here.
80:
81:## Documentation
82:
83:Read `docs/devlog/summary.md` and `docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md` at session start. Key directories:
84:
85:- `src`: app code.
86:- `docs`: architecture, devlogs, reviews, API, tutorials, guides.
87:- `design`: app and mechanism notes.
88:
89:### Discipline (mandatory; not optional)
90:
91:Code changes are not done until the docs match. Before declaring any task complete, run through this checklist for every shipped change. Skipping any item is a regression and will be caught by the next audit.
92:
93:**Always update on every feature / behavior change:**
94:
95:- `docs/changelog.md` ΓÇö new version entry with what shipped, why, validation, and behavior callouts. Audience is external; focus on what users need to know to migrate. Keep dev-internal commentary in the devlog.
96:- `docs/devlog/summary.md` ΓÇö one line per task; remove outdated info; compact if > 50 lines. Do not cheat by writing super long line.
97:- `docs/devlog/detailed/<latest>.md` ΓÇö full per-task entry per the Devlog convention below.
98:- `package.json` ΓÇö version bump per the Versioning convention below.
99:
100:**Always update if the change introduces or removes API surface (new exports, new methods, new types, removed APIs, renamed APIs):**
101:
102:- `docs/api-reference.md` ΓÇö every new public type, method, and standalone utility gets its own section. Removed APIs get removed (not just struck through). Stale signatures must be updated.
103:- `README.md` ΓÇö Feature Overview table mentions the new capability if it's a user-visible feature; Public Surface bullets list the new top-level export if applicable.
104:- `docs/README.md` ΓÇö index links the new guide if one is added.
105:
106:**Always update if the change is structural (new subsystem, new boundary, changed data flow):**
107:
108:- `docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md` ΓÇö Component Map row + Boundaries paragraph for the new subsystem; tick lifecycle ASCII updated if the flow changes.
109:- `docs/architecture/drift-log.md` ΓÇö append a row with date + change + reason.
110:- `docs/architecture/decisions.md` ΓÇö append a Key Architectural Decision row when the change reflects a non-obvious tradeoff worth recording. Never delete an existing decision; add a newer one that supersedes it.
111:
112:**Update if applicable to the change's topic:**
113:
114:- `docs/guides/<topic>.md` ΓÇö every guide whose subject overlaps the change. A new resource API ΓåÆ `resources.md`. A new system feature ΓåÆ `systems-and-simulation.md`. A new spatial primitive ΓåÆ `spatial-grid.md` / `rts-primitives.md`. A new AI-relevant surface ΓåÆ `ai-integration.md`. A new field-data utility ΓåÆ `map-generation.md`. A new tutorial-grade feature ΓåÆ `building-a-game.md` and `getting-started.md`. The `concepts.md` standalone-utilities list and tick-lifecycle ASCII must reflect new utilities and lifecycle changes.
115:- Examples and tutorials must use the current API. If a guide demonstrates the deprecated pattern, replace the demo, don't add a "new way" sidebar.
116:
117:**Verification step (mandatory before declaring task done):**
118:
119:- Invoke the `doc-review` skill or grep for removed-API names across `docs/` and `README.md`. The audit must come back clean for the change's diff. Stale references in historical changelog / devlog / drift-log entries are intentional context and should remain ΓÇö every other surface must reflect current reality.
120:- The multi-CLI code review must explicitly verify doc accuracy as part of its review prompt ΓÇö include "verify docs in the diff match implementation; flag any stale signatures, removed APIs still mentioned, or missing coverage of new APIs in canonical guides."
121:
122:**Why this is mandatory:** doc drift compounds. A single stale signature in `api-reference.md` becomes the source of truth for the next reader, then for the next feature built on top, then for an external consumer. Treating documentation as part of the change (not after the change) is the only way to keep the surface trustworthy. If a feature is too small to merit a guide update, it is small enough to merit one sentence in the relevant existing guide ΓÇö silence is not a valid signal.
123:
124:### Architecture
125:
126:- Respect the boundaries documented in `docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md`. If a boundary seems wrong, flag it instead of silently violating it.
127:- If architecture changes, update the relevant sections in `docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md`, append a row to `docs/architecture/drift-log.md`, and mention the update in the devlog.
128:- Do not update `docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md` for non-structural fixes, refactors, UI tweaks, or test-only work.
129:- Never delete a Key Architectural Decision in `docs/architecture/decisions.md`; add a newer decision that supersedes it.
130:
131:### Devlog
132:
133:- Detailed devlogs live under `docs/devlog/detailed/` as files named `START_DATE_END_DATE.md` (e.g. `2026-04-07_2026-04-13.md`).
134:- A new active file is created with `START_DATE == END_DATE` (today's date for both halves).
135:- Always append new entries to the latest detailed devlog (the file with the most recent `END_DATE`). When looking something up, start from the latest file and work backwards.
136:- Periodically archive: when the active file grows larger than 500 lines or a significant time boundary is reached, `git mv` the file to update its `END_DATE` to the date of its last entry, then start a new file whose `START_DATE` is today (and whose `END_DATE` initially equals `START_DATE`). Check that all previous devlogs' filename dates are still accurate.
137:- After every completed task, append a detailed entry with:
138:  - timestamp
139:  - action
140:  - code reviewer comments, broken down by AI provider and theme as stated above
141:  - result
142:  - reasoning
143:  - notes
144:- Keep `docs/devlog/summary.md` current after updating the detailed log. Always remove outdated info. Compact when it grows larger than 50 lines.
145:- If a subagent handles summary work, it should extract facts only and avoid interpretation.
146:
147:### Versioning
148:
149:- Maintain a version number `a.b.c`:
150:  - Only bump `a` when the human says so.
151:  - Whenever you introduce a breaking change, bump `b` and reset `c`.
152:  - Whenever you introduce a non-breaking change, bump `c`.
153:- **One version bump per coherent shipped change.** Three independent features land as three commits on `main`, each with its own version bump (e.g., 0.5.9 ΓåÆ 0.5.10 ΓåÆ 0.5.11). Do not roll multiple unrelated features into a single version. A single feature that needs iter-1 + iter-2 fix commits stays on the same version ΓÇö the fixes are folded into the original commit's version, not new bumps.
154:- Maintain `docs/changelog.md` with one entry per version. Check `docs/devlog/` for context.
155:- Update the README version badge.
156:
157:### Doc formatting
158:
159:- Don't wrap lines. Only use a new line when you are starting a new paragraph.
160:
161:## Debugging
162:
163:- When debugging, use `docs/debugging/template.md` to record your process. Create a new file per debugging session and use it to iterate until you solve the problem.
164:- If a future session makes you realize that your previous debug sessions on the same topic did not fully solve the problem, update past docs to avoid misunderstandings.
165:- Clean up the temporary files (such as stack dump, test results) created during debugging after you are done.
